Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then heal with tents and other remedies until he is healed.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal, and work, then know that there is a fistula; then treat as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from incision of sword or knife, and it is simple, or deeper, or on the back, then treat as one should with what is before.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large, with stitching; and if it is small, with powder; and if it is pressed into the bone and there are cut pieces, then scrape the wound, and remove the pieces that are loose.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not loose, then let the wound heal, so that it will be bound with ligatures.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and of other wounds on other members is the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly are great, medium, and small.
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	of the great wound sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines are cut, by which the introduction of them.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes it is worse for a small wound than a large one,
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	because one puts the intestines back in more slowly, if one does not put them in little by little.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell as soon as they feel cold, so they enter more slowly.
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and because it is worth more for the medium wound, because one resets the intestine to its place that has other two.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to three manners:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the two common stitches occur in the stitching of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the stitch of other wounds of the body and two other stitches proper are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and yet they are more proper with the stitching of the belly, and I will say each one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestine comes out,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and if something is of the putting back, it is by one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said.
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it up in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	Soak an esponge or one woollen cloth in cold water only.
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or you boil in water, wormwood and cypress, and spikenard,
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and purge the intestine until the swelling is removed.
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes this wine restrains, and is good for only one application to reduce swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling depart, then moisten the intestine with water or ale and have the meadowsweet cooked.
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for by that it is relieved the entrance to a little something;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used to lance hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is good only once the cutting.
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that no one should cut without great necessity, there isn't;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and that is the instrument to split it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	so cut within the curvature and do not force it, and see how it takes shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine springs forth,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	so put it back in its natural place in its proper location,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you have the power, for this is a marvel.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide and it is in the part below the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	so it is necessary that you make the patient sit on their back,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and place his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the part below the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	so place the head and chest higher than the parts below,
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	so position it so that the injured part is higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to follow what I say about great and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	Put these things on small wounds that are pleasing to you,
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then have in your hands one pitiful minister who holds all the rupture in his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and close the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and that is the common method of stitching,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and it is that you take a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave at the head of the wound one or two fingers' space, and insert a needle where there is a good strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two heads of the skin with the two heads of the sphygmachus,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is under the skin inside, as long as you make it pierce from that side,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and tie the two heads of the sphygmachus together in three places;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then strain it with a doubled thread around the needle from both sides,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	and then close the two heads of the wound properly,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave one or two fingers' space, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread as you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not cease to do this until you have need of needles.
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wound is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and be the needles suitable for small and large things,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	because fine needles pierce through all the flesh, and those that are too thick cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore it is necessary that they be suitable;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it is not good to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	for they do not cut and open the wound before the stitching;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut off the heads of the needles so that they do not harm the patient while sleeping.
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I put tents or cloth strips on the heads of the needles to keep them from moving,
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them until the wound is sewn;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because one or two needles are sufficient.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitching method is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you tie the two heads of the skin and the two heads of the sphygmachus together with a needle that has a good strong thread,
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced these heads all three times,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then draw out the needle from the part where you began, in the manner that one sews dresses.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put a space between each stitching, as wide as the breadth of a minor finger.
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitching is suitable for men,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I stitched a wound that a man had on his belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who was wounded by a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm in width.
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and thus were the intestines badly exposed for two palms in width,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I brought back the intestine and it had been outside for 24 hours,
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was stitched up just 15 days later, and I healed it, and it became sound.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctor had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in one place where we could not find any, nor any medicines;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put cotton wool on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was sound.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and push it from the outside part into the inside part;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the skin straight on straight, then tie the head of the sphygmachus or costive to where you have inserted the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the other side of the inside part straight into the outside;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this stitching is that you sew as tailors do with furs,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave the sphygmachus once on one side and then take it up again on the other, until the stitching is all completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of stitching, which Galen says properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is such that some people do, who bring together the two parts naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one of the heads of the sphygmachus to the other head, in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle near the head of the mirach, and make it pierce only that place,
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two heads of the sphygmachus;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle and make it pierce from the outside part into the inside part,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	the second joint of the scrotum;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make two punctures one on each side of the outer part up to the inner part in the two other joints of the scrotum that are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the more usual and common method of stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galens says this saying, and some bear witness to it,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one should sew the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each one;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew leathers;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is inside the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	it is the stitching more difficult than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even if the air has changed it,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	then put back the intestine and the skin; then place on top a powder of burned charcoal,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the air has changed it, then apply some ointment that is present until the wound heals;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and cut off the thread, and sew up the scrotum and the testicles;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as with others, until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you don't have medicine, then apply some old cotton,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you don't need any other medicine for many simple wounds;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound will cause community of the main members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	then it is fitting to anoint with light oil of temperate heat, or with rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and place it around the armpits and under the shoulders;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or burning in his bowels, and many times this happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	then cleanse him with black wine tea, and likewise if the burning comes just to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine which is called "jeune" cannot heal when it is wounded,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and this is because of the plantness of veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of all the body, and the approach of its nature to that of hares.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the intestine jumps out of the wound, then put it back in place just like the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has become green or black, then it is fitting that you bind the place that is black, so that blood does not flow forth,
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then tie off what is between the ligament,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and place the two joints hanging down from the part below the wound up to the outside to facilitate extraction when the intestines fall, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the belly
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	one can restore it in some men,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I have seen a man wounded in the belly by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became covered and turned into a fistula, and from there came the evacuation and belching;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied treatment according to what I could do, and did not cease to subtlety until he was healed, and the wound closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it close, I doubted that the patient had harm in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no harm, but he remained in better conditions, and eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experienced people say that when one has a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take fresh threads from great testicles, then assemble the lips of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the thread has opened the mouth, then place it on the two lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that she strangles her mouth shut;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then tie the knot, and it stays so that he cannot untie it,
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another thread after in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely covered;
et cout la plaie.	and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	This method remains in the intestine, and comes to no harm to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can tie the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the end of this thread of intestine that is well cleaned,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the end of this thread one thread of fine linen twisted,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then put the thread on the needle, and sew up the intestine, and tie it in the rupture;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of stitching with threads is not other than according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, even when it is in one of the larger intestine, then there is no remedy nor health, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or whatever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that any wound or abscess, when it becomes a boil, is universally called "fistula",
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and likewise when it breaks and heals.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And fistula is according to the greenish nodulation of hard and white abscesses, or one does not feel pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it breaks open like the feathers of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it bursts forth suddenly, and other times slowly.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes little, and other times a lot;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed and there is no scar,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	is not other than by one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	to wit, by the smallness of the blood or body;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard scar tissue inside and on the lips that does not allow new flesh to grow.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or if there is too much blood;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the wound is corrupted, and the material is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a manner of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because of the property in the region, digestion is slow and health is delayed, and it flows naturally;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and signs, and cures of medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	And it is necessary that I let you know the treatment for fistula which is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or the spleen, or intestine, or bladder, or some of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or the spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it is to that part which belongs to the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are in this way are of grievous sanitation, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if any fistula does not come just to the point that I have said, and you have faith in the treatment,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you see it clearly, take a piece of iron or bronze, if the fistula is straight, then cut it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is crooked, then search for a subtle piece of lead
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for lead bends to fit around the curvity.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot search it well with tenths,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	then cleanse it through one of the openings,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for the moisture flows quickly from one opening to another, and cleanses it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then cut the bleeding as you are able, knowing whether there is bone or nerve, and it is covered in depth.
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press your hand, and where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you know truly the place where it is, and if it is far from a jointure, or nerve, or artery, or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places I told you, then cut according to what I told you,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and extract the decayed flesh and corrupt char that are inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then treat it until it is healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well founded from a right place, then it is necessary that you cut in depth as far as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then put moistened tents of medicinal aloe, and bind them just to the head of the fistula,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine consumes the superfluity that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then put ointments of sweet salve on clean flesh until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If vein or nerve does not trouble you or principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered and there is corruption and blackness, then remove it all until the corruption is gone.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat with sweet salve until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healed, then do as before.
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you are not yet at the end:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	so uncover and cut until you reach the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot go further;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	so there is no other remedy than to wait for nature's aid.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if it is a small corrupt bone, and you can draw it out with tweezers,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	then extract it with an instrument suitable for this.
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, then remove them all, not leaving even one.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if moisture makes you contrary, and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	then cut and separate the moist flesh and bone, and release the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then put the wound into a poultice of sweet powder.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave it until the flesh is purged around the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then they will have removed more easily.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a great bone, such as one of the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	then remove only the corruption until all the blackness is gone.
puis restoure la plaie;	and then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a great part of the corrupted bone and it comes just to the mold of the bone.
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then it is necessary to scrape and cut all the way to the corruption, and then treat it until it is closed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in a man's leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take it as an example and aid in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man of about 30 years old, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	so that the materials came to the leg and it was inflamed with a big abscess, and there was no other cause by which to open it;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the surgeons, through their foolishness, worked so much that the abscess opened.
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and it was corroding a great deal of matter, and became a fistula, and there came many openings that all poured forth foulness and moisture from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many surgeons put treatments around for two years, and there was no relief in the art of healing,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	so that I was called to it, and saw his leg and the medications by which he was treated.
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and what flowed forth from the openings with great force;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the young man became red and had a yellowish hue.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I placed a tent in one of those openings, and then searched all the openings.
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that one opened into another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hastened then, and cut in one of the openings until I uncovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and it was corrupted and perforated, and the corruption came just to the bone inside.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I cleaned away what appeared from the corrupted bone, and believed that there was no other corruption, except for the one I removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to restore the wound with soothing medicines over a long time, and could not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then recommenced, and uncovered the bone just as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the corruption continued in the bone, and cleaned it, and then removed it, and I made an effort to close the place.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not pull so hard as to pull off about a palm's width from the bone, and then tear it all apart.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored him with medications; and he was healed and bound up quickly.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it did not seem necessary to start the work again except for the patient's weakness, who could not endure.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For often the blood evacuation was painful, but he was healed entirely.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and instead of the bone, a hard callus grew, and he was in good condition with no harm or hindrance from anything at all, neither when lying down nor when getting up.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, then it must be set in this way:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take a ligature and strain it to the top of the exposed bone.
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and instruct someone to pull it up high;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another ligature made of thicker linen than the first one, and tie it above the callus that is over the bone.
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch the top, so that you draw the corrupt flesh down below.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the callus above the place where you want to set it, so that the setting does not harm the callus.
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a hot iron or a wooden splint below the bone to cover the corrupt flesh.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to set it as long as one can see and feel the corruption, and then set it again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part.
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then uncover all the callus; then put a hot iron below,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then set the part from one end of the corruption to the other, and be sure to make the setting a good distance from the length of the corruption as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut out the corrupted joint and set the bone where it contains on the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the connection of the two joints, then there is no other option than to cut it out;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the fingernail of the hand or in the toenail, then that is a very strong thing.
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nonetheless it is necessary for you to ask about this corruption how it appears;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but do not let the vein or nerve hinder you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the incisors and settings for covering these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and their appearance.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and subtlety, and their largeness and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and therefore it is necessary to prepare the instrument for each kind of work.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will show you the instrument that you will need, according to the knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways of diseases.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so prepare the instrument that you need according to what is necessary.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head of the shoulder can become dislocated due to a cause within, or due to a cause outside.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have used medicine to treat that corruption by the cure of medicines, and it does not help.
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	so cover that member up to the place where the corruption comes from.
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient may escape either by death or by the evil of a greater deficiency in the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the sign is that the member becomes black, so that it seems to be burned by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and afterwards it appears as if the blackness had spread from one member to another.
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes hold of everything in the body; and you hasten to cover it.
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if this is due to the percussion of certain venomous beasts, such as the sea scorpion and viper and similar creatures.
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corruption is at the head of the joint, then cut it off, and do not give it any space to reach up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it reaches as far as the hand, then cut it off at the wrist, so that the corruption does not reach up to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it reaches the arm, then cut it off at the shoulder; and if it passes beyond that, it's death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no remedy other than the quantity of his virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and so it goes when the corruption comes to the foot: if it reaches the first joint, then cut it off after the second joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it reaches the foot, then cut off the entire foot.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises to the leg, then cut off at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, then there is no other remedy except to let the patient die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the manner of cutting or setting the member is that you tie it above and below.
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and stretch one minister down with one ligature, and another minister up with the other ligature.
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you uncover the flesh that is between the two ligatures to a spatula-width wide, until the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then cut or set it, and place a linen cloth on each side, so that the setting does not touch the healthy bone.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and another injury and abscess ensues in the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding occurs during surgery, then cauterize the area quickly.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you apply some restraining powders; then return to your medication until it is complete.
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the injured member with a suitable ligature, and care for it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to one man on his sickbed:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a blackness that seemed like burning fire.
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corruption came first to his toe of the foot, until it consumed the entire foot.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corruption, he hastened to cut off the foot, and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long after that, the corruption came back to his finger of the hand, and he came to me.
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put on him things that would rebound after the purification of the body, but the corruption could not cease.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wished that I cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of making the material rebound.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also doubted whether if I cut off his hand, he would not die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the man's vitality was weak; and he became despondent altogether, and returned to his land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and instructs him to cover his hand, and becomes well.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have no other story except that which is made on the other side, if one needs it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	An abscess sometimes comes to a swollen joint, and stays so long that it causes a great gathering of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then bursts and breaks open, and the pus jumps out, and the joint remains empty, just like a vessel.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin above is as subtle as one-eighth of delicate cloths,
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and do not reach all the way to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such diseases are called "stains",
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and is not called a "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it comes all the way to the bone in depth, then it is called a "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is like this: you cut the skin all around, and similarly when it is subtle, just like delicate cloths;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it does not hurt because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have faith that the skin will heal, and the corruption is not in depth,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with fat, then treat it with a poultice thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look and see if the breasts are large, and the abscess that is in them has a foul odor,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then treat it with Egyptian medicine made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take equal parts of asafoetida, oil, and white lead, and put them in one vessel over the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take what you need from this, and mix it with water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and use the poultice to compress the breast, and stop the abscess;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine there for two hours, then strain it by squeezing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times until the breast is healed and the pus is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and sometimes mix with ash water,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and it is that you take ashes of vine wood, and pour water on top,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then let it flow, and use it as a poultice, until you know that the breast is well healed;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot endure this, nor the Egyptian medicine, nor the ash water,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	then mix it with water and honey, or add a little white lead to it;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or use it as a poultice with honey and wine mixed together, so that the honey has the property of healing and cleansing,
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the flesh fresh;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you have faith that the breast is well healed,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	then use a poultice of what causes flesh to grow in it,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and it is that you take diaphanous powder, and mix it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or use it as a poultice of some medicines and ointments, whose properties I have mentioned or to treat with ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the abscess on the breast is small, and the poultice of the clister cannot enter it,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	then enlarge it slightly with a bit of iron, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or Basilikon ointment, until it is enlarged;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too large, then cut and leave it just so that one little part or the poultice can enter,
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the abscess that discharges pus is above, then cut it open or lower it to where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the pus is in depth, one should not allow flesh to remain;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut open the breast below as you see;
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	then prepare it in such a way that the pus runs to the lowest part where it is,
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the pus is deep, one should not allow flesh to remain;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut open the breast below as you see;
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	then prepare it in such a way that the pus flows gently downward, and leave nothing of the pus;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidative medicines to put on the breast,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and place it on one layer of linen that covers the entire breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then cut at the stronger part of the abscess in the breast a little larger than the first,
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then put soft ointment on one more layer according to the size of the abscess;
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and put it on the abscess of the breast to ease the pus, and do not remove the great linen cloth except after a few days once;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and that which is on the abscess of the breast, often removes to remove the pus,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and knows what flows from the pus, whether it is venom or a little or enough, or digested, or indigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take note if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has been thus extended and you see the nature that bursts forth on the abscess of the breast,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	then know that the breast is healed, and approaches health;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then remove it in the morning or the third day, and when you remove the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	then change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast discharges undigested pus after many days, know that the breast is not healed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisons come forth after a long time, do not despair of health;
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for health is approaching. For there are some people whose flesh takes time to heal in their wounds, and others who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if undigested pus bursts forth from the breast after many days, know that the breast is not healed.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breast takes time to heal and becomes inflamed, then add dry medicines that are moist in substance but dry in virtue,
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	like diaphanous ointment, for it contains a great part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take diaphanous ointment, and mix it with rose oil, and equal parts of old wine in substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook and use it; and this same thing makes honey cooked and thickened,
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when diaphanous ointment is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or take mercury and aloes and incense, and grind them together, and powder on the honey when it is on the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then apply one piece of cloth, and stretch it over the chest, and sometimes administer an aromatic substance for a long time,
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of lily of the valley, which is also like wheat of violets and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and in the use of simple or composite remedies: crush them, and make a powder, and put it on the honey I mentioned, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the wound is long and not healed by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then you know that corruption has penetrated deep into the bone, or made a impression on the bones, or caused stiffness in the limbs;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if it is the treatment for fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the tongue
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Furuncle is an abscess that arises under the finger of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or of the foot, or happens by chance in other toes;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is neglected and not taken care of, then a great abscess comes forth,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they run and flow so much that they reach the root of the tongue, and sometimes even all the way to it;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes corrosion right up to the bone, so that there is a foul pain, and the joint of the toe is wide, and the color is fluxed.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	then it is necessary that you cut away all the excess flesh remaining from the tongue,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is a great help if the bone is sound and the tongue is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the tongue then putsrefies the flesh, and begins to prick and bleed,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then it is necessary that you put a cloth under the tongue which pricks the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and tie it up above, and cut away that subtle and delicate flesh.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with oils until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, then cut away the bone, and treat further, for as long as the corrupt bone remains, it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the toe corrupting, then cut it away in one piece as is said before;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is inflamed and swollen, and it feels great pain, then it is necessary that you heal it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut away the tongue of the palate with a crosswise cut above,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and take care that the cut does not come right down to the flesh underneath the tongue, for the patient would feel too great pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then put something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The fingers which are born on some men's hands by chance are all fleshy,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and sometimes there is a bone or a joint.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some of them are born at the root of the joint, or in some of the toes of the feet.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those that are born in any toe of the foot do not move.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those that are born at the joint of the foot, by chance, do move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the fleshiness of one who is fleshy is light, in such a manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at the root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those that are born at the root of the joint are difficult to cure: if you hold off from cutting.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In one who is born or has a bony toe, it is necessary that you cut away the flesh all around to the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone with a suitable thread for this case, then treat until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come together in the toes come from birth, or from a sudden wound, or from burning by fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you cut away the swelling, and then repair the toe according to its natural shape;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two cloths or moistened napkins soaked in rose oil, so that they do not swell.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two thin pieces of linen, until the swelling is settled, as is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a swelling comes on any of his toes with the palm, then cut away that swelling in the same way as before.
Des vils	Of warts
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Warts are great, swollen, and full of melancholy excessences that come on many parts of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they come more often on the legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry loads, rather than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you administer to him at times an evacuation of bile, and then heal with the help of basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The iron treatment is according to two manners: one is when you cut them away, and treat with black blood afterwards;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you lift up the vein, and treat it entirely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cutting is according to this manner: first rise the leg of hot water very strongly, so that the thick blood becomes subtle.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then strain the leg of the patient from above the knee down to the part below the kneecap;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut the vein in one piece, or in two, or in three, with a wide incision,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then lift and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the virtues of the patient can endure.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bind it, and command that he eat food in order to evacuate black bile.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and begin again the evacuation and healing when the veins are full and harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The shaving of him is according to this manner: rise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair.
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put him in a bath, and rise the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and swell the veins.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you don't have a bath, then heat him up over the fire, and then cut away the vein in the long part of the leg at the top of the kneecap, or in the part below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then soak the skin in vinegar, and scrape away the vein from each part, until it is apparent when you touch it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and one can see it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems just like a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	Then tie the thread underneath, until it is raised from the skin, and then pour it onto the scale lightly.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	Then cut into another place on top of three fingers; then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then lift it onto the scale, just as you did, and pour it onto another scale, just as you did first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then cut another size, or as many as you need, then lift it, and cut to the bone of the foot.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then pull and lift just to the second size; then draw it from size to size, until it is all bare, then cut.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	And if you cannot pull and lift it, then tie an awl to each strong doubled thread.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and pull and lift it, and tie underneath one thread, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it doesn't cut, for if it cuts, one cannot pull or lift it, and it will cause harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have pulled it all out, then place wet wool on the wound's bed in wine and rose oil; and care for it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and turned together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	then you must divide it twistedly, but do not cut it; and pull it out just as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of the iron with which one cuts the vein is curved, and does not cut, so it only cuts the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is of great curvature, for if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is the shape:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is situated in legs, in warm regions where there are no herbs nor trees, and in land where there is not a drop of moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and by chance it is found elsewhere than in legs, and this happens due to the purulence that comes from underneath the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	as if it came from within the body as a serpent and moves, situated between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that it comes with a very great inflammation in the leg,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the places change, and the vein begins to come out, just like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the opening is made, then you must envelop around a piece of cloth from one and a half inches to two inches, and bind it.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time it comes to the end, wrap it around the cloth, and bind it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, then cut off a part and wrap the remaining piece, and do not cut off its root until it is all out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it will return to the flesh, and bring abscess and purulence or inflammation at that place, and a bad disease;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	for which reason it is necessary to treat it little by little until the end, and not leave anything remaining in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this vein is treated when it is five palms long or ten,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and one man came to me, from whom it issued ten palms long, and when you cut it, he put a thread or a peg in, and pierced it right down to the bottom,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything comes out; and let the material inside be emptied, and bring medicine to the place to prevent purulence for some time, then care for it just as you would for abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes this vein is treated with many remedies, and especially when it opens at the joint of the foot or in the foot itself,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and it comes out much through openings, and from which springs forth remedies; then care for it just as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of the worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "beef sickness", because it often occurs in oxen.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes up and down through the entire body,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and one can feel it very well as it moves from member to member, until it breaks through the skin where it goes and bursts forth.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by purulence of some humors, such as those that come from worms, serpents, and lumbrii or ascarids in the belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and one doubts of its evil nature, for when it goes through the body and rises to the head, and comes to the eyes.
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance, it enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and pulled out, one cannot avoid but when it moves:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	then it is necessary that you tie the place above and below with a strong tight ligature.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut on top and pull it out, and if the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh, and you cannot find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then cauterize it with fire above, until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the eye at the forehead, then tie a bandage tightly underneath it, then cut on top and pull it out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary to use the patient with a purging medicine for the body's foul humors,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and beware of foods that cause purulence.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and is a pain that comes to some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and it moves from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and about an hour later, I saw it rise up like a worm on the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	quicker than anything else, like bright silver as it cuts from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departed from that place and fixed itself in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then about an hour later it coursed throughout the body, until it came to the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it was twisting around the body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how she moved from member to member in this way, for I had never seen this disease move like that before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had wanted many to move well from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I did not want it, as I saw it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry skin and her veins were uncovered,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and therefore appears that constrained breathlessness;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and do not appear according to this reason to those who are healthy, and who have moist skins and responsive veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you want to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens up as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	so bind above and below hastily, and then cut on top until the constrained breathlessness comes forth.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cautery the place; and if you do not see it to your satisfaction,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	then use a remedy against the breathlessness, such as stinking pills and serpents' pills, and similar others.
Des saiettes	(None)
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the parts of the body where they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of theirs is that there are those which have large points, and small, and barbed, and glued;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those which have two angles, and those which have tongues, and those where there are pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and those that pierce in any member do so in two ways: either the principal member is barbed,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as brain, heart, liver, womb, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it pierces then in any part of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you afterwards, appears:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	so it is necessary that you beware of the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterwards in many conditions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then extract it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the brain sign when the arrow pierces and breaks through the bone, and jumps over the sac that is above the brain,
