est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	which is when there is dimness and dullness and bewilderment and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and commotion of understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it is without force in the nostrils or ears; and perhaps it affects speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and jumps from the moist white wound like pustules, and also as if bruised flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears to you, then hold back from the cure, and do not extract the arrow.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the spleen when it is pierced is that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the spleen becomes as if boils, and in dark black blood, and comes with cold sweat and fainting;
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then know with no doubt that death is certain.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that pierces the womb is when without foam it jumps out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face turns color, and he sighs high and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow pierces the covering of the breast, then it is below the small ribs; and it yields a great deal of pain and great anguish and sighing; and all the members of the shoulders are moved.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow pierces the stomach, perhaps something from undigested food jumps out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow pierces the belly, and in jumping it does not pass through the large intestine, then there is no hope for the cure or the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow pierces the bladder, and urine jumps out and comes forth, and the patient feels very great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulders, and loins of the back, and the ribs, and hips, and legs, and similar members are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you, because I experienced it thus, so that you may do the same.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one man that an arrow fell onto the palm of his hand at the root of his nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it and extracted it from the other side below the ear fat, and he was healed without numbness.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I treated one man who had an arrow in the fatty tissue of his eyelid, just below the eyebrow:
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was lodged and I could only reach as far as the tip towards the wood.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was as long as a Turkish bow, all light iron without ears; the patient was healed, and no bad accident came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I treated an arrow that pierced a Christian from the throat to the ear:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I extracted the barbs and made it subtler until I extracted it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I treated an arrow in one man who had it lodged in his belly, and thought he was dying;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after 30 days, his condition did not change at all;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow, and drew it out, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And I saw one man who had an arrow pierce his back, and the wound was closed above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change his natural disposition.
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor found any harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw one other man who had an arrow pierce his face, and the wound was closed;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remained thus without suffering great pain; and many others were similar.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And I treated an arrow in one of the prince's king who had it lodged near the nose,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly declining to the right side; and the arrow was entirely lodged.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called for the treatment after it had been lodged for three days. I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I sought it with all a subtle tent, and did not feel it.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt a pricking and pain below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the point of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on the skin a plaster of attractive and digestive nature, because the skin does not inflate;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the skin of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on the plaster for many days, and the wound was resolved above, and the patient remained thus for a long time,
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	so that he felt the arrow one day inside his belly; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a medicine of corrosive nature for many days, until it was open.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tried it, and felt the head of the arrow which was stuck to the skin;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I inserted into the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine, until the head of the arrow became visible;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and the edges of the wound healed well in three months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then I opened up the wound so much that I inserted forceps, and pulled it from one side and the other, but could not get it out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I did not stop subtlety and ingenuity with instruments, until I took it one day with well-made forceps,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to the form that will come at the end of this chapter, so I did and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the physicians judged that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was closed, and the patient was entirely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your care on what I do not say, for books cannot learn everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters can take note of very little, and of that which is present and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	and true experience of nine works, and nine instruments, in the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not come out of members where they are stuck except according to two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either through the skin where they enter or from the other side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps out on the other side where it enters is an arrow entering into fleshy parts, and sometimes now jumps out.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump out now, then leave it until the flesh is ripe around, and the issue is freed;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, then leave it so for some days, and move each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it jumps out, and if it does not, then pierce all around with one very fine force, until the skin around is stretched, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes just to one of the vents of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have said happen to the patient: so do not pull it out, but leave it until it is equal after some days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	because if the arrow comes just to the pit of the brain, that's death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not come up to the pit of the brain,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient remains some days without bad accident, then I guide him as to how to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very stuck and cannot come out further, then I administer tarers around, as I have said to you; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is stuck in the flesh of the body so that it cannot be seen, then search for it in every tent.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you find it, then pull it out with any suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot because of the constriction of the wound and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then cut through as much as the wound becomes large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears on which it is stuck.
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	so cut off the flesh that is stuck from both sides to the point where you can;
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow until you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and subtlety well that you do not break the arrow, lest you should pull it out more grievously.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, then leave it until the skin around is ripe, and then pull it out, for the extraction will be freed.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding makes you contrary, then administer what we have said about the cure in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of the incision of the nerve and vein, and put your wit to work on how you can pull out the arrow without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or soon or late, or firmly or gently; and put the patient in the form that he was when the arrow struck him.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for it is the greatest aid that can be; and if you cannot do so, then put him as shown by the sign which shows to you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from the other side, or it appears to be connected to something of it, or the skin is inflamed in the area where one can see or feel it apparently;
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	cut then above, until the forceps can take hold, and then pull it out: if it jumps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, then turn your hand around gently, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then leave it still, and then recommence the extraction until it comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the head of the arrow is stuck in there, then push it all the way to the end.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the head breaks off and you must administer binding, then use one instrument that is beveled;
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters into the bevel of the instrument; and then push forward.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is beveled, then use one instrument with an entering point to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is surrounded by flesh, then it is necessary that you cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as is proper.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow strikes at the hip or at the stomach or at the bladder or at the ribcage, and it is nearby, and you can cut above it, then cut;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and beware of cutting the vein and the nerve, and then pull it out, and then sew up the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and the treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The forms of tweezers used to remove arrows are similar to a bird's beak, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many forms: large, small, and medium-sized, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the comb-like hairpiece is also like a bird's feather,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to push against the tip of the arrow, as follows is its form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of tweezers to push and to grasp if it is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of veins that one cleans oneself, there are .xxxi., of which it has sixteen in the head.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	that is to say: two temples which are after the ears, which are called "herbech";
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two temples appearing;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two corners of the two eyes, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is at the head of the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugulars which are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins one cleans oneself commonly are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and people call it the "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle one is called "faste", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic;
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and people call it the "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and people call it the "vein of the belly", and it is above the scrotum,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is that one that one cleans oneself, which appears manifestly above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the saphena is the vein which is between the auricular and annular, and it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is under the curve of the pocket on the left side,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second saphena which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein that is called "nesse", which is in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are three veins under those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The cleansing of the veins that are after the ears helps ancient catarrhs and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the cleanser, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and wipe the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a screw,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in two small pouches depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	which then goes to your shoulder, and where you feel the pulse under your shoulder, it begins to rise;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lance, and plunge it below the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand along the whole vein upwards,
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and remove the skin and the vein well two fingers' breadth across, and make it bleed until you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then bind and tie it, so that it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said the incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The cleansing of the two arteries that are in the two temples is good for ancient migraines,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and for sore eyes, and habitual blindness, and for tears that flow to the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the cleanser are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient tightens their neck so that the two veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulse under your shoulder, and then begins to rise;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lift the key above the vein at the height of your thumb's first joint, and plunge the lance below.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift the vein high, and cut it, just as you did with the other two veins, and make the wound bleed according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient, and put your thumb on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then bind it firmly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken of their cutting and extraction, in the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The cleansing of the forehead vein is just as good for ancient facial diseases, and for migraines, and for ruddiness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the qualities are that the patient tightens their neck while twisting, so that the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "fossor", which has this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and press down with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then release the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is healed and no longer has a broad inflammation.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not good that the inflammation be too great; and the wound will cross over, for the bone is close, and by chance break through when it is subtle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The cleansing of the two veins that are in the two eyes helps with eye problems, and with itch, and with ruddiness, and with yellowing in the eye, and with facial diseases;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the qualities of their cleansing are that the patient tightens their neck while twisting with some kind of ligature, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then let it bleed, and be the cleansing of the transverse vein, about a finger's breadth long and about as wide, for there is no fat.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the inflammation is subtle, it may break through; then make the wound bleed, as much as you need, and then bind with cotton, and bind well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The cleansing of the nasal vein is good for ague, and for sudden sneezing, and for facial diseases.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	as migraines and ruddiness that come to the face, and especially when they are ancient;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the qualities of the cleansing are that the patient tightens their neck, then presses their nose with your left hand.
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take a thin, long inflammation, and insert it into the space between the two nostrils, in the lip-like fold that is between them.
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	The vein does not open well here, and blood will start flowing now.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too far in depth, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it at night, for it is soon restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the shape of fire:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The juice of two ginsengs helps in the constriction of the gout, and at the beginning of menstruation, and in many diseases, and in impotence, and in corruption, and in herpes, and itching.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the juice is that the patient stretches his neck above one and then the other, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master be standing on the head of the patient, and the patient sits on one seat,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then open the vein of the long one somewhat widely, then let the blood flow temperately, or as much as is necessary.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then do the same on the other vein, then release the ligature, and steady the veins moderately.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient does not choke; and let him sleep until morning, when the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the juice of leaves
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The juice of the veins from the leaves above helps to heal in the mouth, and to corrupt gums, and splits in lips, and around the nose.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	and the quality of the juice is that it makes the patient sit before you, and stretch his neck as I said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left;
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you can recognize them by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	then cut one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then cut the largest one from each side, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the juice under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The juice of the veins that are under the tongue helps after the cephalic juice, and it is for constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the uvula, and for diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the juice is that the patient sits between your hands before the sun, and lifts up his tongue, and looks under each side one black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then cut one and the other, and do not go too far in depth, for underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the back which are commonly bled are bled in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either in piercing with a wide flannel or an olive-like subtle one as the back trenches, and it is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and subtle according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flannel is very well known, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the veins which are smooth and full of thick blood that appears, and contain thick blood and turmoil;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of the olive-like flannel:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtly pointed, and it is for bleeding thin veins, where there is subtle yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The bleeding of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are below the throat, and around the neck, and around the belly, and in the chest;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the doctor to bleed carefully, and to beware of the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and blood comes forth in abundance, then it behooves him to stanch it, as I said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and should not be pierced with the flannel, but cut as anesil.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilic vein does not open clearly, then it behooves you to compress it, and change to another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or else you want some part of it, or you bleed instead in the arm between the veins: it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cut with the flannel as anesil, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to know the place of the bleeding, it behooves you then to compress the arm, that you touch the place until you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place with a pin, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with flannel anesil;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and beware that you do not hit the artery when you see the place swelled, for it is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it flow upwards just like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is arterial blood:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hurry then, and put your hand on high for a long time, then remove your hand if the bleeding stops, as often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	tie up the arm and leave it so, and do not move the patient; and be on watch, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not stopped, and it flows forth, and medical supplies are not present, then cut the artery if it opens, for the head of it retreats; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of linen from the fistula, and cut it, and take one half and tie it on well until the next day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, then treat it as we have said, with powders that stop blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stopping of bleeding is not grievous in many dispositions for the small wound of the plaque, and the power of the ligature of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The bleeding of the vein in the middle helps to treat blood that flows from the head above, and from the body below,
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it behooves the doctor to beware of the nerve that is underneath, and if he pierces too far in depth, and finds the nerve;
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and swells up and the bleeding is grievous, and by chance cannot be stopped.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in some people due to its subtlety, then it behooves you to bleed it with the instrument anesil; and avoid the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, then cut it longwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The brain fluid of the cephalic region helps, which attracts blood from the head, and helps the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to bleed with a vein of the olive or myrtle flame, because this is the most saving of all veins, since there are no nerves nor arteries below.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek out the most level position, and do not disturb anything if it works the first time, and one recommences;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance some people's veins become swollen, so that one must do it once, but it does not cause anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about bleeding, is that bleeding is not done except to preserve health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to prevent diseases from coming;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and let the bleeding be done in one of the three veins that are cut: that is to say, cephalic, femoral, and basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should bleed in the beginning of privations to excess, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of repletion appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one should bleed either the first day or the third day, after two hours or three of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding done for diseases has no fixed time, but when there is need, whether by day or by night, in all hours and at all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not necessary to bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor a woman who is more than four months pregnant up to the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should one bleed those who are very old and have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wants to bleed, in whatever way it may be, it is necessary that he first clears the intestines with a light purgation.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if they have many bad humors retained, so that the veins do not draw out the superfluities from the intestines which are harmful to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor should one bleed those who are too full of meats, nor those who are drunk, until they recover from it, nor those who are dropsical;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and one should not bleed after a colicky passion, and vomiting, and purging of the belly, and multiple times going to bed with a woman, and travail, watching, and fasting, and all such things that make whole virtue, or by something of the arm or body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtly mix the humors, if the blood is thick, by meats and drinks and medicines, if you have the power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then enter or take a bath, if nothing hinders it, to subtlety the blood;
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and bleed from the vein of the liver around the third, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep away from that day all labor, and pain, and lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be quiet and joyful, and let the bleeders be above him whom one bleeds, and press his arm two or three times;
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then loosen the ligature gradually, for if it is too tight or too loose, the blood cannot flow properly;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then press the bandage with one's hands until the veins swell and can be felt;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then moisten the bleeders with the flame of a little old oil, then place his left hand on top of that vein below the bandage a little bit where he wants to bleed;
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not collapse and fail when it is pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flow as smoothly as strings at the time of bleeding, and others that are full of windy emptiness;
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one puts the flame on it, it recoils from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of those;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he opens the vein, it is too narrow, therefore it is necessary that the bleeders be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens at the first attempt, that is good; if not, then one recommences a little below or above that place in haste, if the limb is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limb is swollen and the patient is frightened, one should leave it a day or two, and not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	perhaps an abscess will form; do not enter the bath, then recommence the bleeding if it pleases him;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the incision is small, or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that it will not flow as much as you see, then trust in that very incision itself for all the flame straightway;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and work a little hastily, but so that the limb is swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the limb swollen, do not recommence the bleeding, and put a little of linseed oil on it, for it lightens the body from blood, and is good in this limb where the oil lies.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the linseed oil to each bleeding that you bleed the veins, in order to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and this same thing causes trickling and bleeding from the eyes, when one puts it on the limb; so subtly does it flow and separate when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes a large abscess which often happens, especially when it is not bled too much except at that time or the opening of the vein is small;
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	so hasten, and put on the limb a wet sponge in water and wine, warm a little, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the issue of blood from the vein, and if there remains on the limb after some days any blackness or greenish color, then it will not harm him;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on something with aloe or myrrh mixed in juice of camphor, mastice, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there appears an abscess and swelling at the basilic vein: then put your hand on it, and if you find the limb soft to the pressure of the hand, that is the bad swelling.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not put anything of what we have said on it, for by chance there may be a lack of blood from the artery; but make one application of dry poultice to harden the limb, then treat with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each blood according to its quantity and virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it is thick, let it become thinned out; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for one who is weak and feeble, and has need of bloodletting, that one make a larger wound, and the flaps be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And to one who is feeble, do the opposite, and it is necessary to heal them little by little, and one should heal them by cutting across, not by piercing.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this manner of healing is saved from the corruption of blood and the severing of nerve, and is worth more than long or wide healing.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And to one whose body needs healing, it is necessary to give moist bread soaked in grape juice; if he is fevered, then apply blood-letting three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of a cold complexion, then moisten his bread with a sweet syrup, or with aromatic honey syrup containing spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he vomits after bloodletting, then it is necessary that he drink broth of beef and a subtle, well-scented syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use the other things we have said in the division or chapter of swooning, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to vent his arm and heal another time, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bloodletting, that he heals little by little, according to the quantity of his virtue, continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to vent his arm after the first bloodletting, and he has strong body, then he heals in 7 hours after the first bloodletting, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if one wants to heal from another part, then he should heal on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is much blood inside the body which is already fevered, and brings on fever; so one must draw out a great quantity, and enlarge the opening as far as it can be done.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	and then you will bring together all the conditions of healing, and put your hand on his pulse while he is healing, so that death may not come in place of convalescence.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times when the healer is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it does not happen when you see the arm loosened, and blood coming out the second time, and the opening is closed, that you press strongly on.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	unless he is curved, then let him straighten his arm quickly, for it would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let him stay until he heals the second time; or you come to the tip of the flap, as long as the blood that has congealed at the opening of the vein issues forth,
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on one pouce of silk dipped in water, and press upon it lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is inflamed, then let it be and do not bind it tightly, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires drawing blood the second time, then let it be done in that same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein within the arm is healed in place of the jugular vein because it is compounded.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of healing is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the fleshy part is red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then bind him moderately, so that the vein appears well, then heal him now by cutting across, not by piercing long or wide.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the opening be wide, and let him heal well near the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot come out, then put his hand in hot water, and let the blood run in the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is summer, then do not put his hand in hot water again, for one puts him more at risk of harm in summer than in winter.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the healing of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there is no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The healing of the salvetele of the right hand is worth more than all liver diseases, and this is the manner:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strain the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein is inflamed, so that one can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if it heals across, and if you cut through all of it in all, then nothing will hurt.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not go too far inward, for the nerves are underneath all those strips of flesh,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand in hot water if the blood is congealed in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have let blood as much as is necessary, then put oil and silk on the vein to close it quickly, and thus do for each one.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The healing of the vein on the left hand is worth more for the illness of the mouse, and do all the same as I have told you regarding the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The healing of the sophene is worth more than all diseases that are under the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as diseases of the womb, and retention of flowers, and disease of the kidneys, and old women's hips and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of its healing is that the patient puts his foot in hot water and rubs it on the vein until it breaks.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and lie above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and many rain-like substances go up above the foot.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	heal it then either by opening a larger vein or at the ankle, which is worth more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, then beware of the nerves that are underneath, and let the healing be across as in cutting; and let the flaps be evenly stitched.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water and let it drain well from the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the healer fails the first time, then he should start again the second time a little above, for the flesh is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	nor fear nerves, as we have said, and thus do with the sophene of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The flesh of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of force, and its healing is worth for the pain in the back, when it's due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its healing is that the patient enters or takes a bath, and stretches above the ankle four times by twisting.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it does open, then heal it in all ways you can, and by crossing.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and is worth more than you cut it, for the flesh is sound, and it is very quickly healed by many hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not believe it, then look at any scar of his that appears on the back of the foot or towards the little toe, and beware of nails;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and do so much to stop the bleeding as you see fit, and then loosen the bandage, and put a cloth on it and tighten it; now it is healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Of wounds from cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping-glasses are made of horns, or of iron, or of glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by piercing and attracting blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this cupping that is without piercing is done in two ways: either it is all fire, or not on fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and cupping that is done by piercing and extraction of blood is done in fourteen places of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	whereof one is entirely on the head; and the others are in the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others in the two sides of the neck; and the cupping-glass below the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the cupping-glasses on both shoulders; and the cupping-glasses above the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the cupping-glasses in both arms; and the cupping-glasses in both legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the cupping-glasses on both ankles; and the cupping does not treat blood, unless for small veins that are scattered in the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and therefore one should not faint from it, as one would from bleeding;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not fitting that it be administered, neither with fire nor without fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if, due to necessity of diseases, it is necessary to cup, or for habits, then we should administer each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between, and throughout each period;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are those who, when they need cupping, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are those who become repleted and flushed in their face, and on their head, and at the neck, and darken around the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and there are those who develop a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen the tongue, and bleed;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are those who see visions, and behold by night, and are hurt and wounded and die and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even more so when it is in the middle of the month, we command them to cup after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The bleeding from the nose helps with the swelling of the head... that comes to them, and it is not fitting for this to be done after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this cupping is in place of the bleeding from the head.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it is not fitting for someone who has a cold complexion to use this, or who has catarrh, for this does them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore it is not fitting for the elderly to use this, nor those who have cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who cure themselves often, become forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to put the cupping-glass a little lower down due to the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The cupping on the neck is in place of the bleeding from the head and the basilica, and therefore it is useful for the constriction of the chest.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and for rupture of the channel of the womb, and for all sorts of swelling, and for repletion;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is necessary to use a little force, for if it holds too tightly, it will cause forgetfulness or obstruction of the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The cuppings on the two sides of the neck are worth for pains in the head, and obtalmia, and migraine, and for strangulation, and for pain in the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is in place of the bleeding from the basilica; and it is necessary that you instruct the servant to stretch out his hand when applying it, so that he does not compress the artery, and no blood comes forth.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The cuppings below the chin are worth for mouth diseases, and for corruption of the gums, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it is in place of the bleedings from both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The cuppings on the shoulders are worth for the disease that comes from heat and repletion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The cuppings on the sides are worth as much as the three veins of the arm,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	for it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the servant not to pierce too deeply in front, for the places are bare of flesh, and know that they are beneath the nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping-glass that is on the hip is worth for hemorrhoids of the fundament, and for diseases below, and it is necessary that the cupping-glass be large, and made of iron, so that it can draw well; and by chance, if they were small, they would break; and this makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cuppings on the legs are said to heal obviously, for they draw blood from all the body, and are worth for old pains in the kidneys, bladder, and womb, and restore the flowers; and they take the place of the two Sophene bones and the two ankles, and although they weaken the body after long use, they bring on fainting in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the cupping-glass is that you first empty it, and then apply it with a gentle touch, and place it hastily, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the red and swollen area, and observe the flow of blood; then pierce, and remove the cupping-glasses, and take heed of the condition of the body, for there are those who have thick skin, and clear pores: so it is necessary to strike once only, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and slightly deep ones; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we want to draw out the blood little by little, we should only do it once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood, we should do it often; and if the blood is thick, we should pierce deep and stop when the hearts are pierced suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is necessary for someone who has thick skin and hard, and who have large pores, that you grease the places of the cupping-glasses with oil that is appetizing and dissolving.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in the east, with oil of violets, or with oil of sweet almonds, or with oil of cucumber seed;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is with vinegar, oil of tansy, or of lily, or of chamomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	and if the excesses are big and cold, take bitter oil, or balsamite oil, or wormseed oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	and if the person being cured has tender skin and wide pores, it is not necessary to put oil.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is necessary to wash afterwards with rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or water of gourd, or water of porcelain, or another similar one.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And the one who has too much moisture, should rise up with ease, or with water of myrtle, and of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have big excesses rise up with old wine, or water of sycamore, or a decoction of wormseed or chamomile, or other similar ones.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not necessary to take medicine with a poultice before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for one hour or two; and do not sleep after the purgation.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary that he warms himself when he must be purged and when he is purged.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And take care of the one who is being cured is choleric, and his sweat is too abundant and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	so it is necessary that he takes cold things, such as green apples and endive and lettuce in the morning, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and drink a little, and broth of chicken, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And the one who has a cold complexion, should take honey syrup, and moderately scented wine that is between old and new, and drink little, and drink frequently, and small birds and young pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day he will be purged, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some people sometimes triacle or muscatel before purgation, or after, to comfort the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the sweat be subtle, but it is not necessary that those who are hot drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The poultices that are put to not cause harm are those that are put on the liver, and on the spleen, and on gout, and on the stomach and belly and bowels and behind, for these members do not tolerate being struck or hit.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it is only done to draw blood from member to member.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	such as we put on the breasts when a child is sick; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, just as we put poultices on the stomach and belly to reduce the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it takes away the pain when there is inflammation or stone, and by its attractive virtue, by chance, it draws out the inflammation, or removes the stone from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and thus it does when one puts it on the liver and spleen when there is retained purging.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these poultices are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and at other times with lukewarm water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	such as in diseases of the eyes, and in this manner one fills the poultice with hot water or with water in which herbs suitable for this purpose have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the poultice administered to fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it should be a half-dozen fingers wide and half a palm deep, and have a small hole around the middle one as if to accommodate an awl,
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and it should be made of linen, softened beforehand so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the member.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and it should have in the middle a cross-shaped bar of iron or steel to place a candle upon.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and they should be both large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the poultices of children are different from those of old people, and of thin ones from those of fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should thus place this poultice on the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	take the candle of wax or a linen wick, and place it in the poultice across the bar that is in the poultice,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light may be at the bottom of the poultice so it does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the member, and the edges should be on the hole that we have said, so that when you want to, the vapor goes out, and one removes the poultice.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take up the wick just as before, and keep it going often if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the poultice therefore which is administered in eye disease, it has no bar or hole, and is only used when it is full of water, and is placed on the member alone.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Poultices are only used when there are no other options for members that cannot be treated with poultices because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar parts.
